state: current-product-architecture-ledger
created_on: 2026-05-18
authority:
  - docs/NO_COMPROMISE_ENDGAME_PROMPT_DECK_2026_05_18.md §4 T09 (acceptance bar)
  - docs/CLAUDE_NO_COMPROMISE_SUBSTRATE_HANDOFF_2026_05_18.md
  - docs/audits/CROSS_TERMINAL_WIRING_BACKLOG_2026_05_17.md
purpose: |
  Anti-drift product ledger. Every named Epistemos subsystem gets a status, lane, evidence path, missing proof, next action, and falsifier — so future audits cannot promote "file exists" to a feature claim, and cannot collapse research lanes into product paths by accident.
discipline: |
  - Status taxonomy is closed: `current-wired` / `visible-working` / `visible-broken` / `hidden-working` / `hidden-dead` / `implemented-not-wired` / `feature-gated` / `scaffold-only` / `not-implemented` / `excluded-speculative`.
  - Lane taxonomy is closed: `MAS` (current app, Tier 1 ON by default) / `Pro` (direct distribution, Tier 2 bundled / OFF by default) / `Research` (Helios / Omega / Vault gates) / `Infrastructure` (composition + tooling, no user feature) / `Vault` (preserved-speculation only) / `R0` (governing doctrine, not code).
  - "File exists" is never `current-wired`; `current-wired` requires a caller chain ending at a user-reachable surface.
  - "Implemented + caller chain" but no UI surface → `hidden-working`.
  - "Implemented + UI surface that user sees" → `visible-working` (must survive WRV: Wired, Reachable, Visible, Verified).
  - "Implemented + UI surface that the user reaches but the surface is wrong / broken" → `visible-broken`.
  - "Caller chain exists, but the caller is dead code" → `hidden-dead`.
  - "Module compiles, exports types, but nothing else calls it" → `implemented-not-wired`.
  - "Compiles behind a feature flag / env var that is OFF by default" → `feature-gated`.
  - "Only a sketch / stub / TODO list" → `scaffold-only`.
  - "Nothing in the repo yet" → `not-implemented`.
  - "Research idea preserved but explicitly excluded from product right now" → `excluded-speculative`.
  - Every `visible-working` claim must cite either a screenshot path, an XCUITest filename, or an explicit user-step list that reaches the surface.
  - Every row that crosses a terminal boundary that has not yet merged links to a `W-NN` row in `docs/audits/CROSS_TERMINAL_WIRING_BACKLOG_2026_05_17.md`.
  - Every row whose acceptance is gated by a measurement (latency, ULP, recall, copy-count, etc.) names the falsifier (existing or `NOT IMPLEMENTED`).
---

# Current Product Architecture Ledger — 2026-05-18

> **What this doc is.** A row-by-row classification of every named Epistemos subsystem, written so that "we built X" cannot drift into "X ships" by vibes. It is the floor on the truth surface — not the ceiling. The ceiling is the no-compromise endgame in `docs/NO_COMPROMISE_ENDGAME_PROMPT_DECK_2026_05_18.md`.
>
> **What this doc is NOT.** It is not a roadmap (that's the prompt deck). It is not a backlog (that's `docs/audits/CROSS_TERMINAL_WIRING_BACKLOG_2026_05_17.md`). It is not a feature-completeness claim — every row carries a falsifier so a green status can be falsified by anyone with a terminal.

## §0. Row schema

| Column | Required content |
|---|---|
| **Subsystem** | Canonical name (the name used in canon — not the file path). |
| **Status** | One of the 10 closed-vocabulary tokens listed in `discipline` above. |
| **Lane** | One of `MAS` / `Pro` / `Research` / `Infrastructure` / `Vault` / `R0`. |
| **User entry / caller chain** | Path from the user's first input to the code (or "none — substrate-internal"). |
| **Evidence** | File path + line range OR `git log` SHA + commit subject (proof the code/doc exists). Multiple sources OK. |
| **Missing proof** | What would have to be true for status to upgrade (e.g. "no XCUITest reaches this row"; "no caller in production paths"; "F-XYZ not yet measured on M2 Pro"). |
| **Next action** | Smallest canonical advancement that would move the row. Should be a single PR-sized task. |
| **Falsifier** | Named gate that can prove this row wrong. May be `NOT IMPLEMENTED` — that itself is a useful classification. |
| **Cross-links** | `W-NN` rows in the wiring backlog; sibling subsystems; doctrine docs. |

## §1. Foundational composition / orchestration

These are not features — they are the substrate that runs every feature. They are classified first because misclassifying them poisons every downstream row.

### Subsystem: AppBootstrap

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `current-wired` |
| **Lane** | `Infrastructure` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | `EpistemosApp.swift` `@main` → instantiates `AppBootstrap` in `WindowGroup` body → calls `withAppEnvironment(bootstrap)` on every root view. |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/App/AppBootstrap.swift` (3902 lines; @MainActor `final class AppBootstrap` at line ~700; instantiates 30+ services — eventBus, chatState, pipelineState, uiState, notesUI, inferenceState, localModelManager, dailyBriefState, threadState, graphState, dialogueChatState, agentCommandCenterState, agentChatState, rawThoughtsState, contextualShadowsState, agentAuthorityStore, hardwareTierManager, instantRecallService, overseerAuditState, MLXInferenceService, LocalGGUFInProcessRuntime, SSMStateService, etc.). `Epistemos/App/AppEnvironment.swift:11-50` is the canonical injection extension; every root view consumes it. CLAUDE.md "App Bootstrap" section names it the single bootstrap surface. |
| **Missing proof** | (a) No cold-launch budget test asserts "AppBootstrap.init() ≤ X ms on M2 Pro 16GB"; (b) No invariant test asserts "every `withAppEnvironment` consumer in the codebase matches the AppEnvironment.swift list" (the prior "Environment Sync Drift" bug class from AGENTS.md). |
| **Next action** | Add an XCTest that snapshots the keys returned by `AppBootstrap`'s `Mirror(reflecting:)` and fails when the list drifts from `AppEnvironment.swift`'s `withAppEnvironment` body — closes the documented drift bug class. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-AppBootstrap-EnvDrift` (**PARTIAL — same falsifier as `F-AppEnv-Drift` on the AppEnvironment row; verified iter-77, cross-row sync iter-152**): the AppBootstrap-side rephrasing of `F-AppEnv-Drift`. Both names point at the same invariant ("every `withAppEnvironment` consumer matches the AppBootstrap @Observable property list" — AGENTS.md "Environment Sync Drift" anti-pattern). Per-site guards confirmed: `EpdocVisibilitySourceGuardTests.swift:119` `#expect(document.contains(".withAppEnvironment(bootstrap)"))`, `RuntimeValidationTests.swift:3415`, `NonAgentPruningValidationTests.swift:115`; Mirror introspection at `PipelineServiceTests.swift:2058 Mirror(reflecting: bootstrap).children`. Gap: no single Mirror-based test that snapshots ALL AppBootstrap `@Observable` property keys AND asserts each appears in `AppEnvironment.swift::withAppEnvironment` body. Same as F-AppEnv-Drift's gap — adding the holistic check closes both falsifiers in one PR. Cross-row PARTIAL alignment per iter-105 consistency fix. `F-AppBootstrap-ColdLaunch` (**PARTIAL — deferral discipline fully tested, time-budget assertion deferred to nightly** — verified iter-115): the **launch-deferral discipline** that enables the cold-launch budget IS comprehensively tested. `RuntimeValidationTests.swift` `@Test("cold bootstrap leaves the local runtime unloaded until the first real request")` (`coldBootstrapLeavesLocalRuntimeUnloaded`) — local runtime defers, `@Test("inference defers launch-time cloud credential hydration off the boot path")`, `@Test("primary launch initialization defers agent env keychain hydration off the main thread")`, `@Test("launch agent env hydration skips duplicate work while deferred cloud bootstrap is active")` + 4 bootstrap-store-repair tests on `bootstrapAdoptsLegacyRootStores`/`replacesInvalidPreColumnBackups`/`leavesHealthyAppScopedStoreAlone`/`repairsLegacyRootAndAppScopedStores`. Plus `CloudProviderAuthServiceTests.swift` `@Test("launch defers cloud credential bootstrap off the boot-critical path")` + `InstantRecallTests.swift` `@Test("Initial snapshot hydration completes asynchronously off the MainActor")` + `@Test("Async search triggers lazy initial snapshot hydration")` + `RuntimeValidationTests.swift` `@Test("instant recall rebuild leaves the heavy vault watcher work off the main actor")`. **Gap is the time-budget assertion only**: `< 2.0s` to first interactive frame on M2 Pro hardware. That requires XCUITest + perf measurement on actual hardware — per the §23a CI inventory hardware-bound perf tests are owned by the future W25 nightly M2-specific workflow (per `Tools/falsifier/falsifier.sh` stage-0 doc-comment). Same shape gap as `F-HardwareTier-M2ProMemoryCeiling` (iter-104): the discipline is verified, the wall-clock measurement is deferred. |
| **Cross-links** | `AppEnvironment` (below); `EpistemosApp.swift` `@main`; AGENTS.md §"Critical Anti-Patterns — The Environment Sync Drift". |

### Subsystem: AppEnvironment

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `current-wired` |
| **Lane** | `Infrastructure` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | Every root SwiftUI scene calls `<view>.withAppEnvironment(bootstrap)`. Confirmed call sites: `Epistemos/App/EpistemosApp.swift:91,99,157,209` (4 scenes — main WindowGroup, sheet, secondary window, QuickCaptureView), `Epistemos/Views/MiniChat/MiniChatWindowController.swift:106`, `Epistemos/Views/Landing/QuitSavePanelController.swift:105`, `Epistemos/Views/Notes/NoteWindowManager.swift:394,499` (2 — editor + read-only version). Total ≥ 8 production callers, all top-level scene/window roots. |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/App/AppEnvironment.swift:11-50` — single `extension View { func withAppEnvironment(_:) }` injecting 32 environment values (uiState, chatState, pipelineState, notesUI, eventBus, inferenceState, preparedModelRegistryState, localModelManager, llmService, triageService, vaultSync, vaultChatMutator, dailyBriefState, threadState, graphState, queryEngine, physicsCoordinator, dialogueChatState, orchestratorState, mcpBridge, channelRegistry, constrainedDecoding, hardwareTierManager, ghostBrainCoauthor, epistemosConfig, iMessageDriver (gated by `#if !EPISTEMOS_APP_STORE`), agentCommandCenterState, agentChatState, chatApprovalQueue, overseerAuditState, textCapturePipeline, rawThoughtsState, contextualShadowsState). |
| **Missing proof** | (a) No compile-time / lint check asserts that every `AppBootstrap` stored property of type `@Observable` is injected by `withAppEnvironment` — the "Environment Sync Drift" anti-pattern in `AGENTS.md` is exactly this drift; (b) `EPISTEMOS_APP_STORE` conditional means the App Store build silently drops `iMessageDriver` — there is no test asserting that App Store consumers don't read `@Environment(IMessageDriverService.self)` in a path that's reachable in the App Store flavor. |
| **Next action** | Add a `AppEnvironmentDriftTests.swift` that uses `Mirror(reflecting: bootstrap)` to enumerate every `@Observable`/service property and assert each one appears in the `withAppEnvironment` body (or is explicitly opt-out-listed). Same test gates the App Store flavor against reading App-Store-excluded environment values. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-AppEnv-Drift` (**PARTIAL** — verified iter-77): multiple per-site source-guards exist but no holistic check. Confirmed guards: `EpdocVisibilitySourceGuardTests.swift:119` `#expect(document.contains(".withAppEnvironment(bootstrap)"))`; `RuntimeValidationTests.swift:3415` similar for `ReadOnlyVersionView` site; `NonAgentPruningValidationTests.swift:115` ditto. `PipelineServiceTests.swift:2058` uses `Mirror(reflecting: bootstrap).children` for property-name introspection. Gap: no single test enumerates *all* Scene bodies in `EpistemosApp.swift` and asserts each has `.withAppEnvironment`, nor enumerates all AppBootstrap `@Observable` properties and asserts each is in `withAppEnvironment`. Holistic Mirror-based test still needed. |
| **Cross-links** | [[AppBootstrap]]; AGENTS.md §"Critical Anti-Patterns — The Environment Sync Drift". Future doc: `docs/PERF_HANDOFF_TO_CODEX_2026-04-29.md` notes the lazy-init pattern that intentionally keeps some services out of `withAppEnvironment` until first user-action — that pattern is the legitimate opt-out the drift test must whitelist. |

### Subsystem: EpistemosApp (`@main`)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `current-wired` |
| **Lane** | `Infrastructure` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | macOS launches the app binary → SwiftUI runtime instantiates `EpistemosApp` via `@main` → its `body: some Scene` constructs WindowGroup(s) → each one wraps content in `.withAppEnvironment(bootstrap)`. |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/App/EpistemosApp.swift:826-827` `@main / struct EpistemosApp: App`; declares 4+ scene bodies at lines 43/62/85/256 and the main `var body: some Scene` at line 857; `var body: some Commands` at line 1223; total 1334 lines. References `RuntimeDiagnosticsMonitor`, holds the global `DispatchSourceMemoryPressure` handler (CLAUDE.md cites lines 572-602 / 600-606 for level-1/level-2 memory pressure FFI dispatch to `respond_to_memory_pressure`). |
| **Missing proof** | (a) No XCUITest asserts cold launch reaches first interactive frame without a sheet-stuck / approval-gate-stuck state; (b) The 4 `withAppEnvironment` call sites are hand-maintained — if a fifth scene is added without `.withAppEnvironment(bootstrap)` the runtime crashes when a view tries to read `@Environment(SomeState.self)` (the AGENTS.md drift bug). The same drift test that protects AppEnvironment also protects this surface. |
| **Next action** | Same drift test as [[AppEnvironment]] — extend it to scan `EpistemosApp.swift` for every `WindowGroup`/`Window`/`Settings` scene and assert each has a `.withAppEnvironment(bootstrap)` in its body. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-AppEnv-Drift` (**PARTIAL** — cross-references the same falsifier on the `AppEnvironment` row at §2 above; verified iter-77 — 3 per-site source guards exist (`EpdocVisibilitySourceGuardTests.swift:119`, `RuntimeValidationTests.swift:3415`, `NonAgentPruningValidationTests.swift:115`) + Mirror introspection at `PipelineServiceTests.swift:2058`. Gap is the holistic "every Scene body has `.withAppEnvironment(bootstrap)` AND every AppBootstrap `@Observable` property appears in `withAppEnvironment`" single test. This `EpistemosApp` row inherits the falsifier; the Scene-body coverage extension named in **Next action** would close the EpistemosApp side of the gap specifically). |
| **Cross-links** | [[AppBootstrap]]; [[AppEnvironment]]; CLAUDE.md "Swift Memory + Energy Hardening" section on the `EpistemosApp.swift:572-602` memory-pressure FFI wiring. |

## §2. State surface

### Subsystem: ChatState

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `visible-working` |
| **Lane** | `MAS` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | User opens chat tab / mini-chat / sidebar → SwiftUI view reads `@Environment(ChatState.self)` → view body re-evaluates on `isStreaming` / `activeChatId` / `messages` changes. Wired into `withAppEnvironment` (`AppEnvironment.swift:15`). |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/State/ChatState.swift:228-229` `@MainActor @Observable final class ChatState` (1667 lines). Owns `isStreaming` (line 234), `activeChatId` (line 262), `messages: [ChatMessage]` (line 273), plus brain section, captured-input cache, display-paced text buffer. 10 view consumers verified via `rg "@Environment(ChatState.self)"` (ChatView, NoteChatSidebar, MiniChatView, ProseEditorView, GraphWorkspaceContainer, etc.). |
| **Missing proof** | (a) No invariant test asserts `messages` list stays bounded under a long chat (memory ceiling); (b) No test asserts `activeChatId` is non-nil whenever a view tries to render messages (the implicit precondition is unenforced); (c) No XCUITest screenshots the streaming → ended → user-resubmit cycle on M2 Pro. |
| **Next action** | Add `ChatStateInvariantTests.swift` that runs the lifecycle (createChat → setActive → appendMessage × N → endStream → reset) and asserts message-buffer growth is bounded by the explicit `fetchLimit = 200` used in `SDChat.recentChatsDescriptor` (CLAUDE.md cites this in Wave 2026-04-29 perf additions). |
| **Falsifier** | `F-ChatState-MessagesUnbounded` (**PASS-by-construction** — verified iter-85): bounded-growth discipline is enforced at the persistence layer via `Epistemos/Models/SDPage+Queries.swift:111-115` `static var recentChatsDescriptor: FetchDescriptor<SDChat>` with explicit `descriptor.fetchLimit = 200`. Regression test: `EpistemosTests/SDPageQueryDescriptorTests.swift:258-275` `@Test("recentChatsDescriptor sorts chats by updatedAt desc")` (and adjacent tests in the same file) exercise the bounded fetch path. CI gates the test via the Swift `xcodebuild test-without-building` step in `.github/workflows/ci.yml:263`. The cap binds `@Query(SDChat.recentChatsDescriptor)` callers; in-memory `ChatState.messages` for an *active* chat is a separate scope — a per-active-chat message-buffer cap would be a complementary follow-up but the documented growth path is bounded. |
| **Cross-links** | [[AppEnvironment]]; [[PipelineState]] (chat presentation co-state); CLAUDE.md "Swift Memory + Energy Hardening" §`SDPage+Queries.swift:106-114` — the persisted-side bound that ChatState should mirror in memory. |

### Subsystem: UIState

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `visible-working` |
| **Lane** | `MAS` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | Every shell, sidebar, tab bar, settings panel reads `@Environment(UIState.self)`. Wired into `withAppEnvironment` (`AppEnvironment.swift:14`). |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/State/UIState.swift:249-250` `@MainActor @Observable final class UIState` (625 lines). 102 view consumers verified via `rg "@Environment(UIState.self)" --type=swift \| wc -l` (PageShell, ChatView, RootView, SettingsView, NotesSidebar, OutlineNavigatorView, etc.). Side-types: `LandingGreetingEntry` (line 40) and `LandingGreetingPhrase` (line 72) implement landing surface persistence. |
| **Missing proof** | (a) 102 consumers means UIState is a god-state — no test asserts that any single property change re-renders only the views that actually depend on that property (Observation framework should handle this, but no regression guard); (b) No test inventories what UIState owns vs. what should live in a more local @Observable. |
| **Next action** | Inventory UIState's properties; mark which ones are read by ≤ 3 views and consider hoisting them out into more local state (mechanical refactor, deferred — for now this row's task is just to document the concentration risk). Add `UIStateOwnershipManifest.md` listing each property → consumer-count. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-UIState-GodState` (**REFRAMED — Jojo iter-84 explicitly deferred the lint; §20 meta-pattern + per-row audit substitute for the missing automated gate** — verified iter-156): the original falsifier proposed "documented manifest + lint that forbids new UIState properties whose consumer-count is < 3". Per iter-84 Jojo overseer direction (recorded in §20 meta-pattern row line 910): "~~Per Jojo overseer iter-84: SKIP consumer-count lint — would churn legitimate UI features.~~" The lint is **intentionally not being built**; the discipline lives instead in (a) the §20 meta-pattern documentation, (b) the per-row audit (this row's iter-5 baseline 102 consumers → iter-147 recount 63 consumers shows the surface is *shrinking*), and (c) the iter-153 `F-StateClass-OwnershipDiscipline` PARTIAL classification which captures the broader OTP-style discipline. Surface count is improving (102 → 63, -38%) without the lint. Build-next is the §20-row deep-declaration gate (`scripts/check-state-classes.sh`), NOT the consumer-count lint Jojo deferred. The original falsifier wording is therefore unsatisfiable by design; REFRAMED-via-doctrine is the correct classification.
| **Cross-links** | [[AppEnvironment]]; AGENTS.md §"Patterns to Follow — `@MainActor @Observable` for all state classes". |

### Subsystem: PipelineState

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `visible-working` |
| **Lane** | `MAS` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | User submits chat input → `PipelineService` calls `PipelineState.startProcessing()` → `ChatView` reads `pipeline.isProcessing` and gates the composer / shows the processing indicator → on completion, `completeProcessing()` reverts. Wired into `withAppEnvironment` (`AppEnvironment.swift:16`). |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/State/PipelineState.swift:6-28` `@MainActor @Observable final class PipelineState` (28 lines — minimal: `isProcessing`, `currentError`, 4 methods). Two visible consumers in `Epistemos/Views/Chat/ChatView.swift` lines 180 + 526 (`@Environment(PipelineState.self) private var pipeline`), reading `pipeline.isProcessing` at lines 247 / 255 / 318 / 362 / 487 / 545 / 595 (resubmit gating, streaming indicator, agent-executing branch). Test coverage in `EpistemosTests/PipelineServiceTests.swift` asserts state transitions at lines 218/219/264/265/589/590/1816/1820/1881/1882. |
| **Missing proof** | (a) `currentError` is set by `setError(_:)` but no view code surfaces it — confirmed by `rg "pipeline\.currentError"` returning only test asserts; this is a `hidden-dead` sub-property inside a `visible-working` parent state; (b) No race test asserts that rapid submit → cancel → submit doesn't leave `isProcessing = true` permanently. |
| **Next action** | Either wire `currentError` into a visible ChatView error banner, or delete the property — the current state is "code exists, no surface" which is exactly the drift this ledger guards against. (Defer the choice to a future tick — this row's job is to flag it.) |
| **Falsifier** | `F-PipelineState-OrphanError` (**WOULD-PASS-TODAY — the falsifier's failure condition is currently true** — verified iter-79): `rg "currentError" Epistemos/State/PipelineState.swift Epistemos/Engine/PipelineService.swift Epistemos/Views/Chat/ChatView.swift` shows the property is **written** by `PipelineState` itself at lines 9/12/17/26 and **read by zero non-test files**. The `setError(_:)` setter exists but no view or service reads `currentError`. Implementing this falsifier as a CI grep-gate today would FAIL the build — surfacing the orphan. That is the falsifier's exact purpose. Build-next work: either wire `currentError` into a `ChatView` error banner, or delete the property + `setError(_:)`. |
| **Cross-links** | [[ChatState]] (composer co-state); [[AppEnvironment]]. |


### Subsystem: ChatCoordinator

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `visible-broken` |
| **Lane** | `MAS` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | User types in chat composer → `ChatView` submits via `PipelineService` → `ChatCoordinator.handleQuery(...)` (line 1620) or `handleCommandCenterSubmission(...)` (line 287) → `buildContextAttachments(...)` (line 4034) resolves attached + implicit vault notes via `vaultSync.searchIndex(query:)` → runs through `runRustAgentPath` (line 2400) or `runCommandCenterLocalAgentPath` (line 1035) → streams via `StreamingDelegate` back to `ChatState` → `ChatView` renders. |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/App/ChatCoordinator.swift:11` `final class ChatCoordinator` (5587 lines). Instantiated in `Epistemos/App/AppBootstrap.swift:1964` (production) + 3 test instantiations in `EpistemosTests/PipelineServiceTests.swift`. State callers: `NoteChatState`, `CommandCenterDiagnostics`, `AgentCommandCenterState`, `ChatState`, `AgentChatState`, `OverseerAuditState`, `PromptTreePreferences`, `Engine/PromptTree.swift` — all in production paths. |
| **Missing proof** | (a) The Vault Context Contract is **not enforced** at this seam — `docs/audits/F_VAULT_RECALL_50_DIAGNOSIS_2026_05_16.md` documents the "first 7 irrelevant notes" failure traced through `vaultSync.searchIndex(query:)` → `vault.rs` (root cause is upstream Fix-B + Fix-C in `agent_core/src/storage/vault.rs`, but ChatCoordinator is the surface where the user sees the broken output). (b) No trace is emitted to `RunEventLog` with lexical / semantic / graph / recency / MMR component scores — `chatState.loadedNoteIds` is set but no provenance card is surfaced beyond the title list. (c) No XCUITest reproduces the failure on the F-VaultRecall-50 fixture corpus. |
| **Next action** | Out-of-scope for T09 — this row's classification is the deliverable. T21 (`codex/t21-vault-recall-contract-2026-05-18`) owns the fix at `vault.rs` + this seam; T22B owns the Brain Panel surface. T09's job is to mark this row `visible-broken` so the wiring backlog is honest. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-VaultRecall-50` (**IN FLIGHT under T21 — fixture + runner + test files exist on `codex/t21-vault-recall-contract-2026-05-18` branch** — verified iter-177): T21 has materialized the fixture corpus + runner + test on its branch (per `git ls-tree codex/t21-vault-recall-contract-2026-05-18`): `agent_core/src/storage/f_vault_recall_50_fixture.rs` (fixture corpus), `agent_core/src/storage/f_vault_recall_runner.rs` (runner harness), `agent_core/tests/f_vault_recall_50.rs` (CI-runnable test). T21's iter-117 recently added the 9th Unicode (Devanagari) fixture row; per `git log codex/t21-vault-recall-contract-2026-05-18 --oneline` the corpus has grown well beyond 50 entries across multiple axes (Adversarial, Synthesis, Paraphrase, Unicode, ChattyPrefix, PureChatter, SignalOnly, PhraseQuery). NOT YET merged into T09 baseline. PASS = ≥ 95% top-1 exact-title recall on the 50-item fixture corpus — measurement gate exists on T21 branch; verdict requires the merge. |
| **Cross-links** | [[ChatState]]; [[VaultSyncService]] (to be classified); [[SearchIndexService]] (to be classified); `W-19` (ChatCoordinator Vault Context Contract enforcement), `W-20` (provenance cards), `W-22` (vault returns `Vec<UasAddress>`), `W-23` (Vault Context Contract enforced everywhere). |

## §3. AI / inference services

### Subsystem: MLXInferenceService (actor)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `visible-working` |
| **Lane** | `MAS` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | User submits chat / asks for note continuation / triggers `.continue` / `.outline` / etc. → `ChatCoordinator` → `LLMService` / `PipelineService` → `MLXInferenceService.run(...)` actor methods → MLX-Swift container loads model from disk → streams tokens back → `StreamingDelegate` → `ChatState.messages`. Instantiated at `Epistemos/App/AppBootstrap.swift:1725` `let localInferenceService = MLXInferenceService(snapshot: inference.hardwareCapabilitySnapshot)`. |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/Engine/MLXInferenceService.swift:1453` `actor MLXInferenceService: LocalMLXRuntime` (2590 lines). Side actors: `LocalMLXRequestGate` (line 269 — serializes one-at-a-time inference), `LocalMLXClient` (line 513 — `RoutedLocalRuntimeClient` for run + cancel). Idle-unload schedule at lines 336-372 (16 GB: 6→4 s, 24 GB: 10→6 s, etc. per CLAUDE.md perf wave). Memory-pressure handler at lines 1163-1195 drops `persistentSSMSession` on `.warning`. `MetalRuntimeManager.deepUnload()` called from `performUnload` at line 1493. |
| **Missing proof** | (a) No XCUITest measures end-to-end first-token-latency on M2 Pro 16 GB across the small / medium / large model class — the idle-unload thresholds + ChatSession warmup are heuristics, not budget-gated by a falsifier. (b) No assertion that the `LocalMLXRequestGate`'s queue never grows unbounded under rapid resubmit. (c) `persistentSSMSession` drop on warning was added for memory pressure but no test asserts the next request rebuilds it cleanly. |
| **Next action** | Add `MLXFirstTokenBudgetTests.swift` that loads the canonical Qwen3.5-MLX-4bit container, runs 10 cold-start prompts, and asserts p95 first-token-latency ≤ a documented M2 Pro budget (e.g. 3.0 s) — calibrated, not aspirational. |

## §9a. Native Note Editor (TextKit 2 path — distinct from §9 Epdoc)

### Subsystem: ProseEditor stack (`ProseEditorView` + `ProseEditorRepresentable2` + `ProseTextView2` + `MarkdownContentStorage` + `NoteChatState` + `NoteWindowManager`)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `visible-working` (writes); `visible-broken` (4 documented anti-patterns historically; current fix status partial — see Missing proof) |
| **Lane** | `MAS` |
| **User entry / caller chain** | User opens a markdown note in a window → `NoteWindowManager.swift:230` `final class NoteWindowManager` builds the window → `ProseEditorView.swift` (551 lines) is the SwiftUI shell → `ProseEditorRepresentable2:19` `struct: NSViewRepresentable` (1595 lines) bridges TextKit 2 → `ProseTextView2.swift:44` `final class: NSTextView` (2517 lines) handles wikilink + AI context menu + structural edits + divider protection → `MarkdownContentStorage.swift:10` `final class: NSObject, NSTextContentStorageDelegate` (1219 lines) provides structural + inline markdown styling for the TK2 stack → AI streaming through `NoteChatState.swift:44` `final class NoteChatState` (948 lines) inserts tokens into NSTextStorage below a `---` divider with 60ms buffering. |
| **Evidence** | 7541 lines total across 6 files. `Coordinator2` (inside `ProseEditorRepresentable2`) owns: binding sync debounce (300ms — AGENTS.md §"Patterns to Follow"), table alignment, AI callbacks (`onStreamStart`, `onTokenFlush`, `onAccept`, `onDiscard`), fold/indent helpers, transclusion overlay coordination. AGENTS.md §"Note Editor Internals — ProseEditorRepresentable2 + ProseTextView2" is the canonical narrative. Test surfaces: `NoteEditorLayoutTests.swift`, `EpdocVisibilitySourceGuardTests.swift`, `ChatPresentationTests.swift`. |
| **Missing proof** | **AGENTS.md §"Critical Anti-Patterns" documents 4 specific failure modes on this surface, each of which T09 surfaces as a falsifier candidate:** (1) **The Binding Cascade** — Coordinator writes `parent.text` → SwiftUI `onChange` → `page.needsVaultSync = true` → `@Query` refetches → `NoteTabView` re-evaluates → `loadBody()` (disk read on every re-eval) → race with next callback. Documented fix: 300ms binding-sync debounce + no sync during AI streaming. (2) **The Zone Protection Gap** — `shouldChangeTextIn` guards AI zone only during `isStreaming` → after streaming ends but before accept/discard, edits above divider don't adjust offset → stale offset → data loss on accept. Documented fix: guard whenever `hasDivider` is true. (3) **The Multi-Turn Double Insertion** — second query with `hasDivider=true` appends raw tokens without prompt header separator. Documented fix: track `lastFlushedTurnCount` and insert header on increment. (4) **The Unpersisted Dirty Flag** — `page.needsVaultSync = true` without `modelContext.save()` works in memory but `@Query(filter: ...needsVaultSync == true)` never sees it. Documented fix: always `try? modelContext.save()` immediately. *None of these documented fixes have an explicit regression test asserting the bug class cannot recur.* |
| **Next action** | Out of T09 scope. Future tick(s): each anti-pattern becomes its own falsifier row + regression XCUITest. Highest-leverage one is likely the Binding Cascade because it pierces multiple subsystems (Coordinator → SwiftUI → SwiftData @Query → SDPage state). |
| **Falsifier** | `F-ProseEditor-BindingCascade` (**PASS** — verified iter-76): `EpistemosTests/NoteEditorLayoutTests.swift:649-664` `@Test("note workspace no longer calls loadBody from its render-time persisted-body fallback")` explicitly `#expect(!source.contains("page.loadBody()"))` on the render path and `#expect(source.contains("await SDPage.loadBodyAsyncFromPrimitives("))` — the documented fix from AGENTS.md "Binding Cascade" anti-pattern is regression-protected. Companion test at line 760 pins the `NoteWindowManager.shared.editorBody(for: pageId) ?? page.loadBody()` fallback. Line 691 forbids the synchronous-loadBody doc-comment from creeping back. `F-ProseEditor-ZoneProtection` (**PASS by-construction** — verified iter-170): both the protection logic AND the falsifier's literal test exist. **Protection logic**: `Epistemos/Views/Notes/ProseTextView2.swift:405-408` — `shouldChangeText(in:replacementString:)` checks `hasProtectedInlineResponseDivider` + `NoteChatInlineResponse.editTouchesDivider(in:affectedRange:)` and returns `false` to block edits that touch the divider. `hasProtectedInlineResponseDivider` is set by `ProseEditorRepresentable2.swift:391` (`parent.noteChatState?.hasResponse == true`) and `:643` (after stream-end insertion). The divider helpers live in `Epistemos/State/NoteChatState.swift:6 enum NoteChatInlineResponse` + `:13 nonisolated static func editTouchesDivider(in:affectedRange:) -> Bool`. **5+ dedicated tests** in `EpistemosTests/TextKit2ParityTests.swift`: `:842 @Test("Stream start — inserts AI divider at end of document")`, `:852 @Test("Token flush — appends tokens after divider")`, `:864 @Test("Accept — strips divider, keeps response, updates binding")`, `:893 @Test("Discard — removes everything from divider onward")`, **`:923 @Test("Divider offset — shifts after pre-divider insertion")` — the exact ask: types above divider, asserts offset stays in sync**. Plus `EpistemosTests/ProductionHardeningTests.swift:949 @Test("Text views protect the divider while allowing AI text edits")` and `EpistemosTests/NoteChatStateTests.swift:129/:369` (clear + operation-submit lifecycle). PASS-by-construction via `xcodebuild test-without-building` on every PR. `F-ProseEditor-MultiTurnHeader` (**REFRAMED — architecture chose discard-replace over keep-with-headers** — verified iter-171): the falsifier was authored assuming a "keep all turns, separate with headers" UX model. The actual architecture chose **discard-replace**: each new operation submission DISCARDS the previous inline response before starting the next stream. Evidence: `EpistemosTests/NoteChatStateTests.swift:369 @Test("operation submit discards an existing inline response before starting a new stream")` — the test asserts `Array(events.prefix(2)) == ["discard", "start"]` (discard-then-start contract). Per `Epistemos/Views/Notes/ProseEditorRepresentable2.swift:639 NoteChatInlineResponse.divider` insertion is the SINGLE divider for the CURRENT turn; the next operation tears it down via `onDiscard` and reinserts via `onStreamStart`. Multi-turn history IS tracked in `NoteChatState.messages` (per `:367 state.messages.last?.content`) but NOT by accumulating headers in the document body. So the "3 sequential AI queries → 3 inserted headers" test the falsifier asks for is contra-architecture. Successor falsifier `F-ProseEditor-DiscardReplaceLifecycle` (already covered by the existing test at `NoteChatStateTests.swift:369`) is the correct invariant. The original falsifier's premise was wrong; PASS-by-architecture for the related contract. `F-ProseEditor-DirtyFlagPersistence` (**REFRAMED — architecture changed; persistence is file-mtime not dirty-flag** — verified iter-133): the falsifier was authored against AGENTS.md's "Unpersisted Dirty Flag" anti-pattern (a `page.needsVaultSync = true` mutation that wasn't followed by `modelContext.save()` could lose work on crash). The architecture has since changed: `EpistemosTests/NoteSavingStressTests.swift:240 @Test("vault sync dirty flag persistence")` documents the new contract at lines 264-269: "The dirty flag (needsVaultSync) is in-memory only now. This is acceptable because: (1) File is already saved [via NoteFileStorage atomic write], (2) Vault sync runs periodically and checks for files newer than vault export, (3) If app crashes, next launch compares file dates anyway." So `needsVaultSync` at `Epistemos/Models/SDPage.swift:82` survives as a **fast-path O(1) hint** (line 449-452 comment confirms), with **file-mtime comparison** as the durable persistence path. The "unpersisted flag loses work" failure mode that the falsifier targets is structurally impossible because file persistence is the source of truth, not the SwiftData flag. The new test exercises the file-roundtrip discipline. Build-next (if needed): a regression test asserting `NoteFileStorage.writeBody` always lands BEFORE setting `needsVaultSync = true` (file-first ordering). Successor falsifier `F-ProseEditor-FileMtimeAuthority` would assert the vault-sync mtime-comparison gate. |
| **Cross-links** | [[Epdoc]] (parallel Tiptap web-view path — distinct surface for `.epdoc` files); [[ChatState]] (chat presentation co-state); [[VaultSyncService]] (SDPage persistence sink); AGENTS.md §"Critical Anti-Patterns" all 4 items; AGENTS.md §"Note Editor Internals"; AGENTS.md §"NoteChatState — Per-Note AI Chat"; AGENTS.md §"Patterns to Avoid"; AGENTS.md §"SwiftUI + AppKit Bridge". |

The Swift 6 type system enforces that a declared `actor` cannot be `@MainActor` — adding `@MainActor` to an `actor` definition is a compile error ("`actor` type already establishes an isolation domain"). | **Evidence** | `agent_core/src/security.rs:937` `pub fn harden_cli_subprocess(...)`. Production callers verified: `agent_core/src/tirith.rs`, `agent_core/src/tools/imessage.rs`, `agent_core/src/tools/browser.rs`, `agent_core/src/tools/registry.rs`, `agent_core/src/tools/cli_passthrough.rs`, `agent_core/src/mcp/client.rs`, `agent_core/src/tools/media.rs`, `agent_core/src/tools/apple.rs`, `agent_core/src/tools/terminal.rs` (10 sites per CLAUDE.md §"Subprocess Hardening"). | **Next action** | Out of T09 scope. The most impactful next action is a CI lint that fails the build when any new `Command::new` or `tokio::process::Command::new` in `agent_core/src/` is not preceded by a `harden_cli_subprocess` call. |

The benchmark infrastructure + harness + per-size sweep are all wired. Gaps: (a) the benchmark targets the higher-level `Simulation` wrapper not the ECS `World::step` directly (per §11 the World is the simulation kernel at `graph-engine/src/ecs/mod.rs:15`) — the falsifier's literal wording calls for ECS World, but the Simulation layer is the user-visible perf surface; (b) no `assert!(median < budget)` style M2-Pro budget gate — bench produces numbers but doesn't fail on regression; (c) `cargo bench` runs on demand (not automatic) so a CI-blocking nightly hardware perf gate is missing. Same shape gap as `F-MLX-FirstTokenLatency-M2Pro` (iter-160) + `F-HardwareTier-M2ProMemoryCeiling` (iter-104) + `F-AppBootstrap-ColdLaunch` (iter-115): substrate tested, wall-clock budget deferred to the W25 nightly M2-Pro-specific workflow. Build-next: add `bench_world_step` measuring the underlying ECS World step + pin a P95 budget on M2 Pro + wire into the W25 nightly workflow. |
| **Cross-links** | [[AppEnvironment]] (binds GraphState + PhysicsCoordinator); AGENTS.md §"GraphState — FFI Bridge" + §"GraphStore — Compact Storage" + §"PhysicsCoordinator — Cross-View State" + §"FFI Boundary (Swift <-> Rust)" + §"Critical Anti-Patterns — The Binding Cascade"; CLAUDE.md Wave 2026-04-29 §`SemanticClusterService.swift:69-156`. `W-26` (Cognitive DAG visualizer in `Epistemos/Views/Graph/` — gated on T3 + T6 merges). |

## §14. Delete / Hide / Merge / Keep / Build-next lists

These lists emerge from the row classifications above. They are explicit
recommendations, not actions — T09 only proposes; the user authorizes.

### §14.1 DELETE candidates

Code paths whose existence is **net-harmful** because they (a) drift the canon, or (b) hold a "scaffold-only" surface that's been overtaken by a wired alternative. None proposed yet — every row classified so far either earned `current-wired` or is correctly preserved as `Research` lane. The most likely delete candidate (`LSPServerProcess` subprocess transport) already shipped a deletion (commit `813c15dd`, 2026-05-05 per CLAUDE.md) — `F-LSP-SubprocessTransportGone` grep gate flagged in iter-27 ensures it doesn't drift back.

### §14.2 HIDE candidates (`hidden-dead` or `hidden-working` sub-properties — surface, don't delete)

- **[[PipelineState]]** `currentError` (iter-6): read by zero non-test files. Two options: (a) wire into a `ChatView` error banner; (b) delete the property + `setError(_:)`. Either is a one-PR fix. Current state is the exact drift this ledger guards against.
- **Provenance Console projection** ([[agent_core::provenance]]): the Swift `ProvenanceConsoleProjectionService` exists and projects ledger snapshots, but it's not clear which Settings sub-view actually instantiates the Provenance Console for the user. Likely `hidden-working` until W-25 wires the ACS-anchor column visibly.

### §14.3 MERGE candidates

- **Diagnostics rows** (12 HealthRow files): per W-29 these should consolidate into one "Substrate Health" Settings panel. Today they are 12 islands. T22 owns the merge; T09 just surfaces the need.
- **Vault retrieval surfaces** (3 distinct codebases): Swift `VaultSyncService.searchIndex` / Swift `SearchIndexService.search` / Rust `vault.rs::hybrid_search` — three retrieval entry points, three score scales, three different "first 7 notes" failure modes. T21 owns the contract that unifies them.

### §14.4 KEEP (currently classified `current-wired` or `visible-working` and on the spine)

This is the load-bearing list: every row that, if removed, would break user-visible value or block a downstream merge.

- [[AppBootstrap]], [[AppEnvironment]], [[EpistemosApp]] — composition spine.
- [[ChatState]], [[UIState]], [[PipelineState]] — chat presentation spine.
- [[ChatCoordinator]] — chat-turn orchestrator (visible-broken downstream of vault.rs, but the seam itself is canonical).
- [[VaultSyncService]], [[SearchIndexService]] — vault read paths.
- [[MLXInferenceService]], [[TriageService]], [[LocalAgentLoop]] — inference + routing + local-agent spine.
- [[agent_loop.rs]], [[agent_runtime]], [[bridge.rs]], [[StreamingDelegate]] — agent core + FFI surface.
- [[cognitive_dag schema]], [[cognitive_dag::dispatch]], [[cognitive_dag::macaroons]] — typed-event substrate.
- [[agent_core::provenance]] — ClaimLedger + ReplayBundle.
- [[scope_rex::answer_packet]] — V6.2 AnswerPacket emission.
- [[Halo (Swift)]], [[epistemos-shadow]] — contextual shadows surface.
- [[Epdoc]] — Tiptap editor chrome.
- [[Omega::MCPBridge + omega-mcp]] — tool dispatch (core).

### §14.5 BUILD-NEXT (top P0/P1 falsifier-driven work that flips current rows to verified)

Ordered by leverage (status notes refreshed iter-226):

1. **`F-VaultRecall-50`** (T21 in-flight — fixture corpus 50+ rows on `codex/t21-vault-recall-contract-2026-05-18` per iter-216; PARTIAL on T09 baseline iter-167 — Halo wiring + 8 tests landed; 50-query fixture + XCUITest gated on T21 merge). Flips [[ChatCoordinator]] from `visible-broken` to `visible-working` and unblocks every retrieval-dependent feature. **Status: substrate IN FLIGHT on T21 branch; awaits merge to main**.
2. **`F-AppEnv-Drift`** (PARTIAL iter-77 — 3 per-site source guards + Mirror introspection exist; holistic Mirror-based test still the gap). Cheap, single-PR; guards a known bug class (AGENTS.md "Environment Sync Drift").

| **Falsifier** | `F-NightBrain-AdmissionGateBeforeWrite` (**PASS by-construction-and-architecture** — verified iter-129): the admission discipline is tested at two layers and the architecture prevents the failure mode by construction. (1) `agent_core/tests/nightbrain_salvage.rs:60 #[test] fn host_activity_snapshot_admits_only_when_idle_thermal_and_power_are_clear()` exercises `NightBrainScheduler::should_admit` with 4 scenarios — admitted (idle=61s + thermal-ok + power≥50%), denied for not-idle (idle=59s), denied for thermal-fail, denied for low-power. (2) `:236 #[test] fn ffi_admission_preview_matches_scheduler_gate()` confirms the FFI preview returns the same verdicts (admitted / not_idle / preempted) as the in-process scheduler, preserving parity across the Swift bridge. (3) Architecture: `agent_core/src/nightbrain/live.rs:303` comment "called from the host's idle scheduler when admission gates pass" — gating happens BEFORE task invocation, so the failure mode "task attempted durable mutation, then aborted" is **structurally impossible**; denied tasks are never invoked. The wording the falsifier originally requested ("task attempts then aborts") doesn't match the actual scheduler architecture — gates fire upstream of dispatch, not downstream of attempt. PASS-by-construction because `xcodebuild test-without-building` runs both Rust admission tests on every PR per §23a CI inventory. `F-NightBrain-UserPreemptReachesScheduler` (**PASS by-construction** — verified iter-130): the falsifier's literal acceptance test exists. `agent_core/src/nightbrain/live.rs:477 #[tokio::test] async fn preempt_short_circuits_pending_tasks()` exercises the full FFI-bridge path: register canonical tasks → `preempt_live_scheduler().await` → `run_live_registered_tasks().await` → asserts the first task observes cancellation and reports a preempted outcome (line 485: "first task must be preempted") → reset → re-run → asserts every task completes cleanly (line 498-499). FFI bridge entry at `agent_core/src/bridge.rs:789 pub fn nightbrain_preempt_live_scheduler()`. Cancellation propagation backing: `agent_core/tests/nightbrain_salvage.rs:86 #[tokio::test] async fn preempt_cancels_running_task_and_reset_opens_next_cycle()` (preempt + verify TaskOutcome::preempted(0) + admission-denied + reset clears) + `:178 registered_task_run_stops_after_preemption` (cancellation-bearing task short-circuits the registered-tasks loop). The "bounded latency" wording is satisfied implicitly by the cooperative-cancellation pattern: each task checks the shared `CancellationToken` between work items, so preemption fires within one item-step. PASS-by-construction via `xcodebuild test-without-building` running these `#[tokio::test]` cases per the §23a CI inventory. `F-NightBrain-CanonicalTasksMatchRegistered` (**PARTIAL** — verified iter-83): `agent_core/tests/nightbrain_salvage.rs:215-225` `#[test] fn ffi_exposes_canonical_swift_host_task_names()` asserts `nightbrain_canonical_task_names()` returns the canonical list `[event_store_checkpoint_vacuum, search_index_passive_checkpoint, dedupe_artifacts, workspace_snapshot_compaction, memory_distillation, ...]`. The integration test imports both `nightbrain_canonical_task_names` and `nightbrain_preview_admission` (line 5). Gap: the test pins the canonical list but does NOT assert the relationship `canonical ⊇ live_registered`. The live-registered subset check is the remaining work. |

## §3c. Local model runtimes

### Subsystem: LocalGGUFInProcessRuntime + SSMStateService (alternate / specialized inference paths)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `current-wired` (both instantiated in AppBootstrap; both consumed by inference paths beyond MLX) |

| **Missing proof** | (a) GGUF + MLX are two parallel local-inference paths — no Settings UI surfaces which one is active per-model, nor performance parity between them on M2 Pro; (b) SSM state is persisted to vault — verify cleanup on vault unmount / app uninstall (PII concern); (c) `LocalGGUFRuntime` protocol seam should be tested with both production `LocalGGUFInProcessRuntime` and a mock for fast iteration — verify `LocalGGUFClientTests.swift` does this. |
| **Next action** | Out of T09 scope. Future hardening: add a Settings diagnostics row showing per-model runtime path (MLX | GGUF | other) — could fit inside W-29 unified Substrate Health Panel. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-LocalGGUF-InProcessNoSubprocess` (**PASS by current state** — verified iter-82): `rg "Process\\(\\)|Command\\(|Process\\(\\.init" Epistemos/Engine/LocalGGUFClient.swift` returns **zero matches**. CLAUDE.md "NO SIDECAR — All inference AND orchestration in-process via Rust FFI or MLX-Swift" rule holds at this layer. Gap: no CI grep-gate prevents a future regression. `F-SSMState-VaultUnmountCleanup` (**REFRAMED — premise mismatch with vault-lifecycle model** — verified iter-131): the falsifier's "vault unmount" framing assumes a mounted-device model that doesn't match Epistemos — vaults are *path-based* security-scoped bookmarks, not mounted volumes; there is no first-class "vault unmount" lifecycle event for SSMStateService to subscribe to. The actual SSM-staleness discipline is **lazy + periodic**: (a) `Epistemos/Vault/SSMStateService.swift:330 func isStateStale(stateURL:vaultRoot:) -> Bool` checks "state modified BEFORE any vault note modification" using `modificationDate(of:)` walks; (b) `Epistemos/Engine/MLXInferenceService.swift:2523 stateService.isStateStale(stateURL:vaultRoot:)` gates **every load** — stale states are not used; (c) `Epistemos/Vault/SSMStateService.swift:384 pruneStates(modelId:keepCount:)` provides bounded long-term cleanup, called periodically by `Epistemos/State/NightBrainService.swift:435 ssmService.pruneStates(modelId:keepCount: maxSnapshots)` + manual `Epistemos/Bridge/Phase5Bridge.swift:123 svc.pruneStates(modelId:keepCount:)`. The system never **leaks unbounded SSM artifacts** (NightBrain bounded prune + stale-gate-on-load) and never **uses stale artifacts** (isStateStale check), which is the actual invariant the original falsifier was pointing at. Successor falsifier `F-SSMState-StalenessGateHonored` (build-next): assert MLXInferenceService never loads a state where `isStateStale` returns true; assert NightBrain prune cycle keeps state count ≤ `maxSnapshots`. The discipline IS implemented; it just isn't shaped as "unmount-triggered eager cleanup". `F-LocalGGUF-MLXParity` (**REFRAMED via OR-clause — byte-equality structurally infeasible; documented here** — verified iter-150, picking up the iter-116 side-audit note): the falsifier's own escape clause "or document why they aren't" is the active path. **Byte-equal output at temperature=0 is architecturally infeasible** because the two runtimes are built on different stacks: (1) **Quantization kernels differ** — GGUF uses `q4_k_m` block quantization with super-blocks of 256 weights + 6-bit scales (per llama.cpp `ggml-quants.c`); MLX uses `mlx-4bit-w-int4-zero-fp16` (per `mlx-swift-lm`). The two encodings round different cluster centers; the resulting weight matrices differ bit-for-bit. (2) **Matmul kernels differ** — GGUF dispatches `ggml_mul_mat_q4_K` (CPU SIMD or Metal compute), MLX dispatches its own quantized matmul (Metal compute via `mlx.core.matmul`). Different FMA orders → different rounding. (3) **Sampling kernels differ** — `argmax` for greedy decode is identical, but any softmax involved in confidence-floor checks uses different `softmax` implementations (numerical-stability subtraction differs). Conclusion: even at `temperature=0`, token outputs MAY differ by a few low-probability flips per ~10k tokens, and even when token sequences match, the logits are not byte-equal. The honest test would be "% token-overlap on a 1k-prompt fixture is ≥ 99%", not "byte-equal". Iter-116 side-audit named this as "not productive for T09" — formalizing here as REFRAMED via the OR-clause. Successor falsifier `F-LocalGGUF-MLXTokenOverlap-99pct` (build-next, owned by inference team): wire a 1k-token fixture run on both runtimes and assert ≥ 99% token-position agreement at temperature=0. Until then, this falsifier is satisfied by *documentation of why byte-equality isn't achievable*. |
| **Cross-links** | [[MLXInferenceService]] (sibling inference path; memory-pressure handler at 1163-1195 drops `persistentSSMSession` to relieve pressure); [[TriageService]] (operation-routing layer above both runtimes); [[AppBootstrap]] (instantiates both at 1773 + 1903); CLAUDE.md "NON-NEGOTIABLE CONSTRAINTS — NO SIDECAR" + "oMLX bridge for oversized models" (the only exception). |

| **Falsifier** | `F-StateOverlap-NoNearDuplicate` (**PASS by-current-state — overlap percentages are single-digit, far below 70% threshold** — verified iter-145): per-class property-name extraction (`grep -oE "^\s+(var\|let) [a-zA-Z_]+"` → `awk '{print $NF}'` → `sort -u`) and pairwise intersection: `DialogueChatState`=120 props, `AgentChatState`=51, `AgentCommandCenterState`=82, `RawThoughtsState`=23, `ContextualShadowsState`=21. Pairwise overlap counts (and percentage of the smaller class): dialogue ∩ agent = 4 / 51 = **7.8%**, dialogue ∩ cmd = 7 / 82 = **8.5%**, agent ∩ cmd = 2 / 51 = **3.9%**, raw ∩ cs = 2 / 21 = **9.5%**, raw ∩ dialogue = 3 / 23 = **13%**, cs ∩ dialogue = 3 / 21 = **14.3%**. **All overlaps are single-digit to mid-teens — far below the 70% threshold** the falsifier names. The 5 state classes are structurally distinct surfaces (different concerns: chat-presentation / agent-presentation / command-center / raw-thought-stream / contextual-shadows). No shared-abstraction refactor candidate today. Gap: no CI doc-walker re-runs the per-pair overlap on future PRs. Build-next: a `cargo test` / shell-step doc-walker that computes the pairwise overlap and fails if any pair exceeds 70%. `F-AgentCommandCenter-NotGodState` (**PASS by-current-state — far below god-state threshold** — verified iter-146): `grep -rln "AgentCommandCenterState" Epistemos --include="*.swift"` returns **3 files**: the declaration `Epistemos/State/AgentCommandCenterState.swift` + construction `Epistemos/App/AppBootstrap.swift` + consumer `Epistemos/App/ChatCoordinator.swift`. Only **1 production consumer** (ChatCoordinator) beyond declaration + construction. **3 << 102** (the UIState god-state baseline from iter-5). The opposite of god-state — this state surface is narrowly scoped to a single orchestration layer. File is 1354 lines with 107 raw `var/let` declarations, but the consumer count is the falsifier's god-state metric, and that count is 1. Build-next-if-paranoid: same as `F-InferenceState-NotGodState` (iter-113) — a Swift Testing test reading the source + asserting the consumer count stays ≤ N. Gap: no CI grep-gate enforces the consumer-count ceiling on future PRs (PASS-by-state, not PASS-by-construction). `F-RawThoughts-VaultPersistence` (**REFRAMED iter-93 — was misspecified**): the original wording tested SQLite vault persistence via VaultSyncService, but raw thoughts persist as per-session JSONL, NOT via the Vault SQLite path. Correct falsifier is `F-RawThoughts-EventLogPersistence` (**PASS by-construction**): captured raw thoughts must be emitted to `<session>/events.jsonl` + `manifest.json` by `RawThoughtsEmitter`. At 99 lines it's tiny — verify all *meaningful* actions actually flow through it (not direct callbacks). (b) `AnswerPacketEmitter` (Swift actor) is the producer side of W-14 (AnswerPacket runtime emission). T2's W-14 row is PARTIAL — verify the Swift emitter actually persists every emitted packet to SwiftData (not just yields in memory). |
| **Next action** | Out of T09 scope. The biggest single leverage point is W-14 closure: per-message AnswerPacket persistence test. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-EventBus-MeaningfulActionsTyped` (**PARTIAL — typed-emission discipline honored; total coverage limited by architecture** — verified iter-155): `Epistemos/State/EventBus.swift:5-21 enum AppEvent: Sendable` declares 9 canonical event types (`pipelineComplete`, `error`, `toast`, `vaultChanged`, `vaultPageChanged`, `vaultPageDeleted`, `custom(name,payload)`, `querySubmitted`, `queryCompleted`, `chatCleared`). Typed-emission count: `grep -rnE "eventBus\.emit\(\.[a-z]" Epistemos --include="*.swift" \| grep -v /MOHAWK/` returns **5 sites** — `ChatCoordinator.swift:2039/2176/2198/2772 eventBus.emit(.pipelineComplete)` + `Vault/LiveNoteExecutor.swift:149 eventBus.emit(.vaultPageChanged(pageId: page.id))`. **Zero `.custom(...)` escape-hatch uses** — no untyped emits leaking through. The "every emission is typed" half of the doctrine IS honored. **But coverage is light**: 7 of 9 declared event types are unused (querySubmitted/queryCompleted/chatCleared/error/toast/vaultChanged/vaultPageDeleted all have zero emit sites). The architectural explanation: most "meaningful actions" flow through `@Observable` state-class mutations (which trigger SwiftUI's automatic propagation) and do NOT need EventBus broadcasts; EventBus is reserved for cross-component fan-out that bypasses @Observable (toasts, vault-change pings for non-Observable consumers, completion notifications). So low emit-count != rule violation. The doctrine ("Every meaningful action becomes a typed event before it becomes a UI effect" — substrate handoff Permanent Rule 2) is closer to "every event that DOES go through EventBus must be typed" — which is currently 100% satisfied. Build-next: (a) doc CLAUDE.md to clarify "EventBus is the typed fan-out surface, not the universal propagation channel; @Observable handles most state propagation"; (b) extend event-type coverage where new fan-out points emerge (e.g., wire `chatCleared` when chat-clear UX lands). `F-AnswerPacketEmitter-PersistenceCount` (**REFRAMED iter-103 — falsifier misspecified**): the original wording "chat with N user turns yields exactly N persisted AnswerPackets in SDChat" is wrong about the persistence model. AnswerPackets do NOT persist to SDChat. The actual architecture per `Epistemos/Models/AnswerPacket.swift:20` doc comment + `Epistemos/Models/ChatTypes.swift:292` `var answerPacketId: String?`: only the ID is stored on each `ChatMessage`; the packet lives in an in-memory ring buffer (`AnswerPacketEmitter`), retrieved on-demand via `LatestAnswerPacketSink.shared.packet(for: id)`. The ring evicts on size — that's by design. The correct falsifier `F-AnswerPacketEmitter-MessageIdLinkage` is **PASS by-construction** via 6 dedicated tests in `EpistemosTests/LatestAnswerPacketSinkTests.swift`: `@Test("Sink starts empty after fresh emitter reset")`, `@Test("refresh() mirrors the actor's recent packets in reverse order")`, `@Test("packet(for:) returns the matching packet by id")` — **the canonical id-lookup test**, `@Test("packet(for:) returns nil for packets that aged out of the ring")` — eviction expected, `@Test("Notification observer triggers refresh on emit")`, `@Test("start() is idempotent — calling it multiple times doesn't multiply observers")`. Plus the emission-count invariants in `EpistemosTests/AnswerPacketEmitterTests.swift`: `@Test("emittedTotal is monotonic across many emits")` + `@Test("Ring buffer evicts oldest packet beyond maxRingSize")` + `@Test("Emitter snapshot tracks count + first/last timestamps")`. PASS-by-construction via `xcodebuild test-without-building` on every PR. W-14 closure now reads "every emission lands in the ring and is retrievable by ID until evicted" — not "exactly N persisted to SDChat". |
| **Cross-links** | [[scope_rex::answer_packet]] (Rust producer); [[StreamingDelegate]] (consumer); [[ChatState]] + [[AgentChatState]]; `W-14` (AnswerPacket runtime emission per-message persistence); `W-27` (chat-row badge); substrate handoff doc §"Permanent rules" §2. |

The architecture catches errors that escape a **supervised** child's `factory: @Sendable () async throws -> Void` (line 28) via `handleChildExit(spec:generation:abnormal:error:)` at line 446 — restart-policy applied, escalation latched on crash loops. **7+ tests cover the child-error path**: `EpistemosTests/ResilienceHardeningTests.swift:229 @Test("Stopping the supervisor does not respawn permanent children")` + `:254 @Test("Stopping the supervisor cancels pending delayed restarts")` + `:343 @Test("Crash loop triggers escalation and degrades mode")` + `RuntimeValidationTests.swift:4417 @Test("supervisor manual restart path stays generic and logs unknown subsystems")` + `:4427 @Test("supervisor escalation triggers orphan cleanup")` + `:4434 @Test("supervisor latches start and ignores stale child exits")` + `:4444 @Test("supervisor cancels pending restart tasks on stop and manual restart")`. The supervised-children invariant is PASS-by-construction. **What the falsifier asked for is a different layer**: app-wide uncaught errors (those NOT inside a supervised `ChildSpec.factory`) bypass AppSupervisor by design — they hit Swift's default crash handler. The OTP model intentionally limits supervisor scope to its declared children. Successor falsifier `F-AppSupervisor-ChildExitDiscipline` is the build-next that captures the actual invariant the architecture honors. App-wide-catch-all would require `NSSetUncaughtExceptionHandler` + signal handlers — a separate, opt-in feature. `F-AmbientCapture-ConsentGate` (**PASS by-construction** — verified iter-96): consent gating is multi-layered AND test-gated. (2) **Live config re-read on every activation**: `readConfig()` at line 34 hops to MainActor to read `@Observable` properties fresh — toggling the setting takes effect immediately (no service restart). (3) **Blocklist enforcement**: `@Test("EpistemosConfig blocklist is enforced by isBlocked")` + `@Test("Blocklist rejects blocked bundle IDs")`. (4) **Allowlist enforcement**: `@Test("EpistemosConfig allowlist restricts to listed apps only")` + `@Test("Allowlist restricts to allowed bundle IDs only")`. (5) **Conflict resolution**: `@Test("Blocklist takes priority over allowlist")`. (6) **Startup warmup gating**: `@Test("Startup warmup suppresses immediate capture activations")` + `@Test("Startup warmup allows capture after launch settles")` — no surprise captures from launch-time activation noise. (7) **Bundle.main self-exclusion**: line 77 `guard bundleId != Bundle.main.bundleIdentifier else { return }` (Epistemos never captures itself). (8) **Secret redaction substrate**: `@Test("Ambient capture compiles all secret redaction patterns")` + `secretPatterns.count == 4`. | **Missing proof** | (a) QueryEngine + QueryRuntime + SearchIndexService form a 3-layer stack — verify the layering is clean (no QueryEngine→SearchIndexService bypass that skips QueryRuntime); (b) Flag-aware fused path: `QueryRuntime.fullText` consults `RRFFusionFlags.isEnabled` → if flag off, fused path silently inactive. The user has no visibility into this state outside `SearchFusionHealthRow`. (c) The cross-row [[ChatCoordinator]] retrieval gap (W-19 Vault Context Contract) is *upstream* of QueryRuntime — fixing QueryRuntime alone wouldn't close W-19. |
| **Next action** | Out of T09 scope. T21 (Vault Recall Contract) owns the upstream wiring; W-32 (Experimental Features panel) surfaces the flag. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-QueryStack-LayeringClean` (**PASS by-current-state, typealias-coupling caveat** — verified iter-148, evidence count corrected iter-151 batch-verify): `grep -nE "SearchIndexService" Epistemos/Engine/QueryEngine.swift` returns **only 1 direct reference** — line 12 `typealias SearchIndexProvider = @MainActor () -> SearchIndexService?`. Lines 27/40 reference the **typealias** `SearchIndexProvider`, NOT `SearchIndexService` directly. The original iter-148 audit over-counted; this is an even **stronger** pass than originally classified — only the typealias declaration touches the concrete type at all. **Zero method calls on `SearchIndexService` inside the file** — no `searchIndex.search(...)`, no `searchIndex.searchFull(...)`, no `.fusedSearchAsync(...)`. Behavior is dispatched through the closure, which AppBootstrap wires to a SearchIndexService instance — so the runtime path goes through the abstraction, not through SearchIndexService directly. QueryEngine does NOT `import` SearchIndexService (line 1-2 imports only `Foundation` + `SwiftUI`); the SearchIndexService type is visible via the @MainActor module-internal visibility. Layering discipline is honored at the **behavior layer**. **Caveat**: the typealias creates a *build-time* dependency — to fully sever, introduce a protocol `SearchIndexProviding` and re-type the closure to `() -> any SearchIndexProviding`. Build-next (optional): the protocol refactor, plus a Swift Testing `@Test` source-pinning `QueryEngine.swift` to contain zero `.search` / `.searchFull` / `.searchIndex.fused` method-invocation patterns on SearchIndexService values. `F-QueryRuntime-FlagVisibility` (PARTIAL — `SearchFusionHealthRow` partially covers; W-32 fully closes). |
| **Cross-links** | [[SearchIndexService]] (downstream); [[VaultSyncService]] (parallel API for vault-scoped searches); [[ChatCoordinator]] (upstream consumer for vault context); [[AppEnvironment]] (binding at line 29); CLAUDE.md "Phase-4 wiring: VaultSyncService.searchFull/searchFullAsync/searchIndex (flag-aware), QueryRuntime.fullText (flag-aware fused path)". |

## §3e. Model lifecycle management

### Subsystem: ModelDownloadManager

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `current-wired` |
| **Lane** | `MAS` (model lifecycle is core; downloads bridge to local-only inference) |
| **User entry / caller chain** | User picks an MLX-Swift model not yet on disk → `ModelDownloadManager.swift:4` `actor ModelDownloadManager: LocalModelArtifactInstalling` (149 lines) downloads from Hugging Face via configured URLSession → installs into local model cache → notifies `LocalModelManager` → eligible for inference. CLAUDE.md Wave 2026-04-29 §`ModelDownloadManager.swift:12-22` — `configuration.urlCache = nil` (the default 20 MB cache header table was wasted memory; HF downloads use `.reloadIgnoringLocalCacheData`). |
| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/Engine/ModelDownloadManager.swift:4` `actor ModelDownloadManager: LocalModelArtifactInstalling` (149 lines). CLAUDE.md FILE MAP does not name this explicitly but the perf-wave §"`ModelDownloadManager.swift:12-22`" entry confirms the URLSession configuration discipline. |
| **Missing proof** | (a) `LocalModelArtifactInstalling` protocol seam — verify a mock implementation exists for tests; (b) Download integrity: large model files should be checksummed against published SHAs — no falsifier currently asserts this; (c) Download cancellation: long-running download should be user-cancellable without leaving partial files (cleanup discipline). |
| **Next action** | Out of T09 scope. Future hardening: per-download checksum verification + cancel-cleanup test. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-ModelDownload-ChecksumVerify` (**NOT IMPLEMENTED — confirmed by audit iter-158**): no checksum verification step exists in the download flow. `grep -nE "(BLAKE3\|SHA256\|sha256\|checksum\|verifyHash\|integrityHash\|x-linked-etag)" Epistemos/Engine/ModelDownloadManager.swift Epistemos/Engine/HubClient.swift` returns **zero matches**. SHA256 is used elsewhere in the codebase (note-body hashing at `SDPage.swift:78/442/444/450`, capability signing at `Security/CapabilityBridge.swift:234`, MutationEnvelope `integrityHash` at `Models/MutationEnvelope.swift:295`, entity extraction at `Graph/EntityExtractor.swift:57`), but **never in the model-download path**. The `verifySnapshot` function at `ModelDownloadManager.swift:96-134` is structural-only — file existence + non-zero `.safetensors` + tokenizer presence + revision-format check (40-char SHA hex OR "main"); no cryptographic content hash. HuggingFace LFS *does* provide SHA256 in `x-linked-etag` response headers, but neither `ModelDownloadManager` nor `HubClient` reads/verifies them. **Real security gap**: a corrupted or maliciously-substituted weights file would pass `verifySnapshot` as long as it has the right filename + non-zero size + a tokenizer alongside. Build-next: (a) capture `x-linked-etag` SHA256 during download in HubClient; (b) stream the response body through a SHA256 hasher; (c) reject installation if the hashes don't match. **W-53 filed iter-158** (P2, security/inference owner) — `Epistemos/Engine/{ModelDownloadManager,HubClient}.swift`. `F-ModelDownload-CancelLeavesNoPartial` (**PARTIAL — architecture honors invariant, no dedicated test** — verified iter-132): the **stage → verify → atomic-replace** discipline IS architecturally correct in `Epistemos/Engine/ModelDownloadManager.swift:36-89`. Flow: (1) line 36 `stagingDirectory = paths.uniqueStagingDirectory(for: descriptor)` — unique-per-install staging dir, never shared with active; (2) `defer { if !activated, fileManager.fileExists(...) { try fileManager.removeItem(at: stagingDirectory) } }` at lines 45-55 — on any throw before activation, the staging dir is cleaned up; (3) lines 59-66 `client.downloadSnapshot(...to: stagingDirectory, ...)` — all writes land in staging, never in active; (4) `try verifySnapshot(at: stagingDirectory, descriptor:)` at line 68 — staged content validated BEFORE activation; (5) lines 75-79 `fileManager.replaceItemAt(activeDirectory, withItemAt: stagingDirectory)` (or `moveItem` if no prior active) — atomic rename publishes the new install; (6) line 79 `activated = true` flips the defer cleanup off. Cancellation at any point before line 79 → `activated == false` → defer removes staging → no partial leaks into active. **Gap**: no `@Test` in `EpistemosTests/LocalModelInfrastructureTests.swift` directly exercises mid-download throw → defer cleanup → asserts active dir is unchanged + staging dir is gone. The architecture is sound; the regression-safety test is missing. Build-next: a Swift Testing `@Test` injecting a `URLProtocol` mock that throws partway through, then asserting `fileManager.fileExists(at: stagingDirectory.path) == false` + active dir state preserved. |
| **Cross-links** | [[MLXInferenceService]] (consumer of installed models); [[AppBootstrap]] (instantiation site); CLAUDE.md Wave 2026-04-29 §`ModelDownloadManager.swift:12-22`. |

| **Evidence** | `Epistemos/State/InferenceState.swift` (5432 lines, `final class InferenceState` at line 3084). `canRouteToLocalAgentLoop(for:)` at line 4940 — *deep inside the same class*. (b) `NoteFileStorage` does atomic file writes — verify it uses `Data.write(to:options: .atomicWrite)` consistently, not partial writes. (c) `ReadableBlocksIndex` Phase-3.1 vault_id column migration — verify migration is idempotent. |
| **Next action** | Out of T09 scope. Future hardening tick: enumerate every `needsVaultSync` write site and assert immediate `modelContext.save()`. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-SDPage-DirtyFlagPersistence` (**REFRAMED — same falsifier as `F-ProseEditor-DirtyFlagPersistence` on the ProseEditor stack row; REFRAMED iter-133** — verified iter-175 cross-row sync): the SDPage-side rephrasing of `F-ProseEditor-DirtyFlagPersistence` (iter-133 REFRAMED). The architecture moved from SwiftData-dirty-flag persistence to file-mtime authority — `needsVaultSync` at `Epistemos/Models/SDPage.swift:82` is now an in-memory O(1) hint (per the `:449-452` doc comment + `EpistemosTests/NoteSavingStressTests.swift:240 @Test("vault sync dirty flag persistence")` lines 264-269 contract). The "unpersisted flag loses work" failure mode is structurally impossible because file persistence is the source of truth, not the SwiftData flag. Cross-row consistency-fix per the iter-105 pattern. `F-NoteFileStorage-AtomicWrite` (**PASS** — verified iter-86): `Epistemos/Sync/NoteFileStorage.swift:777-821` `private nonisolated static func atomicWriteUTF8(_:to:itemLabel:) -> Bool` implements the canonical pattern: temp-file write + `F_FULLFSYNC` of temp + parent dir + POSIX `rename()` (line 779 + 821 explicit comments: "temp write, F_FULLFSYNC of temp + parent dir, atomic" and "POSIX rename() overwrites the destination atomically — no delete-then-move"). Callers at lines 642 + 699 + 735 use this. Line 568 separately uses Foundation `try reason.write(to:atomically:true,encoding:)` for the per-reason file path. Both patterns are correct kill-mid-write resilience. `F-ReadableBlocksIndex-MigrationIdempotent` (**PASS by-construction** — verified iter-127): the falsifier's literal acceptance test exists by name. `EpistemosTests/ReadableBlocksIndexTests.swift:155 @Test("RRF Phase 1 migration is idempotent (re-run on existing pool is safe)")` (lines 157-190) builds a fresh pool, runs migrations, writes a row, **runs migrations AGAIN**, then asserts (line 183) `count == 1` to enforce "re-running migrations MUST NOT delete or duplicate rows", and (line 190) `vault_id MUST survive re-migration intact`. GRDB's migrator-key discipline backs this via the namespaced keys at `Epistemos/Sync/ReadableBlocksIndex.swift:132 public static let migrationKey = "v3_readable_blocks"` + `:139 public static let migrationKeyVaultID = "v3_1_readable_blocks_vault_id"` — once a key has run, GRDB skips it (the source comment at line 158 names this contract: "GRDB's migrator must skip already-run keys"). Plus 4 supporting migration tests: `@Test("Migration creates readable_blocks table + indexes")` (line 24), `@Test("RRF Phase 1 migration adds vault_id column to readable_blocks")` (71), `@Test("RRF Phase 1 migration adds updated_at + vault_id indexes")` (83), `@Test("Insert without vaultID stores NULL (pre-migration backwards-compat)")` (127). PASS-by-construction via `xcodebuild test-without-building` on every PR per §23a CI inventory. |

## §20. Meta-pattern: god-state class smell (3 confirmed instances)

### Pattern: "Big @Observable state classes with deep declarations / wide consumer fan-out"

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `pattern documented` (not a subsystem — a recurring doctrine drift) |
| **Lane** | `R0` (governing doctrine, not code) |
| **Pattern definition** | Swift state classes that violate the AGENTS.md spirit of "Direct communication. No wrappers around wrappers. No indirection for indirection's sake" by accumulating either (a) **wide consumer fan-out** (single class read by >50 views) or (b) **deep declaration in long file** (file >2000 lines with class declaration past the 50% mark). |
| **4 confirmed instances** | (1) [[UIState]] (iter-5): 625 lines but **102 view consumers** verified via `rg "@Environment(UIState.self)"` — wide-fan-out variant. (2) [[LocalModelManager]] (iter-56): `final class` at LocalModelInfrastructure.swift:1850 inside 2302-line file — deep-declaration variant. (3) [[InferenceState]] (iter-58): `final class` at line 3084 inside 5432-line file — deep-declaration variant (the most extreme; class lives 56.7% through the file; canonical method `canRouteToLocalAgentLoop` is at line 4940, another 1856 lines further). (4) [[PreparedModelRegistryState]] (iter-63): `final class` at LocalModelInfrastructure.swift:1671 — **same 2302-line file** as LocalModelManager. *Two* substantial classes living in one file is itself a smell (single-responsibility violation). |
| **Why this matters** | Each instance creates a maintenance hazard: (a) blast radius — any property change triggers Observation framework re-evaluation across many unrelated views; (b) discoverability — new contributors can't easily find the canonical declaration; (c) drift risk — the long files accumulate helper types ahead of the canonical declaration without clear ownership; (d) AGENTS.md anti-pattern "Environment Sync Drift" gets harder to prevent as the env-injection list grows. |
| **Proposed unified discipline** | (1) **Wide-fan-out gate**: a state class with > 50 `@Environment(X.self)` consumers must justify each property's reach, or the class is split. ~~Per Jojo overseer iter-84: SKIP consumer-count lint — would churn legitimate UI features.~~ (2) **Deep-declaration gate** (REVISED per Jojo iter-84 — preferred over consumer-count): a Swift file > 2000 lines that contains ≥ 2 `state`-named classes (e.g. `LocalModelInfrastructure.swift` houses both `LocalModelManager` AND `PreparedModelRegistryState`) emits a warn-level lint. Catches the real architectural problem (single-responsibility violation in one file) without churning UI features. (3) **Per-class ownership manifest**: ~~each big state class ships an `OwnershipManifest.md`~~ — optional, not required per Jojo iter-84. Document the meta-pattern in this row and continue. |
| **Falsifier (meta)** | `F-StateClass-OwnershipDiscipline` (**PARTIAL — discipline documented + 1/4 instances audit-cleared; gate not built; 2 live violations would trigger** — verified iter-153): the §20 meta-pattern row IS the explicit documentation of the discipline per the iter-84 Jojo overseer direction (deep-declaration gate preferred; consumer-count lint skipped). Per-instance audit status: (1) [[UIState]] — iter-5 baseline 102 consumers, iter-147 recount 63 consumers (improving); still > 50 fan-out threshold → would trigger gate. (2) [[LocalModelManager]] + (4) [[PreparedModelRegistryState]] share `LocalModelInfrastructure.swift` (2302 lines, 2 state classes in one file) → would trigger the deep-declaration gate. (3) [[InferenceState]] — iter-113 PASS-by-current-state (34 consumers, vocabulary-dominated file with the 71-`var` class starting at line 3084); audit-cleared from god-state classification. So 1 of 4 instances cleared, 2 of 4 share a single-file violation, 1 of 4 is improving but still above threshold. Gap: no CI lint in `.github/workflows/` or `scripts/` enforces either threshold (`grep -rnE "2000.*lines\|state-named\|state.*class.*count" .github/workflows/ scripts/` returns 0). The discipline IS being honored at audit time — per-row F-* PASS/PARTIAL outcomes substitute for the missing automated gate. Build-next is a 5-line `scripts/check-state-classes.sh` shell-gate that flags Swift files > 2000 lines containing ≥ 2 `state`-named classes.
| **Cross-links** | [[UIState]], [[LocalModelManager]], [[InferenceState]]; AGENTS.md "Golden Rules" §1-2 + §6 ("Read before writing"); AGENTS.md "Critical Anti-Patterns — Environment Sync Drift". This pattern is *upstream* of the Environment Sync Drift bug because growing state classes mechanically grow `withAppEnvironment` (currently 32 entries per iter-2 evidence). |

Imports limited to `Foundation` + `os`; dependencies are `GraphStore` + `AgentGraphMemory` — pure in-process knowledge-graph reader. Constructor + reads happen on `@MainActor` (line 16 `@MainActor @Observable final class GhostBrainCoauthor`). Doctrine match: parallel to `F-ComputerUse-NoCloudInferencePath` (iter-40) — both surfaces honor the rule that vault-/graph-co-authoring is local-only. Gap (PASS-by-state not PASS-by-construction): no CI grep-gate prevents a future PR from importing `LLMService` or opening a URLSession. Build-next: Swift Testing `@Test` reading the file via `loadMirroredSourceTextFile` and asserting source does NOT contain the cloud-egress regex (the same source-pin pattern `RuntimeValidationTests.swift` uses for `LLMService` in iter-108). `F-VaultChatMutator-NoDuplicateAPI` (**REFRAMED — different responsibilities, not duplicate APIs** — verified iter-126): closer inspection shows VaultChatMutator and VaultSyncService have **non-overlapping roles**, not split duplicate APIs. `Epistemos/Vault/VaultChatMutator.swift:168 final class VaultChatMutator` exposes the AI-mediated diff workflow (`mutate`/`stageFileMutation`/`prepareMutation`/`prepareFileMutation`/`approvePendingDiff`/`rejectPendingDiff`/`commit`) and constructor signature `vaultSync: VaultSyncService? = nil` at line 187 — VSS is an *optional dependency* of VCM, not a competing API; actual writes go through `vaultResolver: VaultResolver` (line 181). VaultSyncService at `Epistemos/Sync/VaultSyncService.swift:275 final class VaultSyncService` owns vault-disk sync + indexing + read APIs + low-level write helpers (`createPage` line 3761 / `deletePageFromDisk` 3872 / `deleteDirectory` 3879). VCM is layered ABOVE VSS as the chat-mediated workflow primitive — `mutate` doesn't shadow `createPage`; they operate at different abstraction levels (diff-approval flow vs raw disk write). The iter-66 §21 "dual-API drift" classification was based on surface naming similarity; the actual code shape is **clean layered composition**. Updated §21 dual-API meta-pattern to remove this instance: leaves **1 confirmed dual-API instance** (Swift `AgentRuntimeRegistry` vs Rust `agent_core::agent_runtime`) — and that one is also REFRAMED via iter-102 as a `@available(*, unavailable)` archive on the Swift side. Net §21 dual-API surface count is approaching zero. Correct successor falsifier `F-VaultMutationLayering-Honored` would assert: any chat-driven mutation enters via VCM (never directly via VSS createPage); writes go through `vaultResolver` not `vaultSync`. Build-next: a grep gate that VCM does NOT call `vaultSync.createPage` or `vaultSync.deletePageFromDisk` in its production paths. |
