## §21. Meta-pattern: dual-API / competing-identity drift (3 confirmed instances)

### Pattern: "Two subsystems that overlap in responsibility but have separate codepaths"

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | `pattern documented` (R0 doctrine, not code) |
| **Lane** | `R0` |
| **Pattern definition** | Two named subsystems with **overlapping responsibility** but **separate implementations**, both currently in production. The risk is per AGENTS.md Golden Rule §1 "Zero copy-paste" + §2 "Direct communication. No wrappers around wrappers." — competing identities create drift surface, divergent behavior under concurrent edits, and split test coverage. |
| **2 confirmed instances** (iter-79 correction: was 3; AppCoordinator/AppBootstrap pair removed after audit) | (1) **VaultSyncService vs VaultChatMutator** (iter-8 + iter-63): both mutate vault state. `VaultSyncService.swift` (4257 lines, `@MainActor @Observable final class` at line 274) is the canonical vault read+write surface; `VaultChatMutator.swift` (809 lines) is a separate mutator specifically for chat history. The split is plausible (chat-history mutations have different invariants than note mutations) but un-documented — verify chat-vault writes always go through `VaultChatMutator` and not via `VaultSyncService`'s broader API. (2) **AgentRuntimeRegistry (Swift, iter-55) vs `agent_core::agent_runtime` (Rust, iter-15)** — **RESOLVED BY COMPILE-TIME DEPRECATION (iter-102 audit)**: Swift `AgentRuntimeRegistry` is marked `@available(*, unavailable, message: "Archived compatibility surface. The shipping app routes agent sessions directly through ChatCoordinator and LocalAgentLoop.")` at `Epistemos/Engine/AgentRuntime.swift:93`. Any caller that touches it fails to compile with the documented redirect. The 116-line Swift class is a compile-time archive; Rust `agent_core::agent_runtime` is the only LIVE surface. **The collision is dead-class drift, NOT a live competing identity** — the doctrine clarity goal is met by language-level enforcement. Counts as a confirmed §21 instance for historical / discoverability reasons (someone reading old commits will encounter the Swift symbol) but it is not a live failure mode. (Removed: **AppCoordinator vs AppBootstrap** — iter-79 audit showed AppCoordinator is a user-action orchestrator that *consumes* AppBootstrap-instantiated services, not a competing composition root.) |
| **Why this matters** | (a) New contributors don't know which API is canonical → write code against the wrong path, diverging behavior; (b) Bug fixes land in one path but not the other → "fixed last week" becomes "still broken on the other path"; (c) Test coverage splits, lowering net safety; (d) AGENTS.md Golden Rule §1 "Zero copy-paste" is violated by mechanical duplication when both surfaces grow in parallel. |
| **Proposed unified discipline** | (1) Every confirmed dual-API instance must have a **canonical-path doc** identifying the primary surface and the *legitimate* reason for the secondary surface (different invariants, threading, namespace, etc.). (2) **Deprecation gate**: a dual-API with no legitimate reason becomes a deprecation candidate — one is marked `hidden-dead` and prepared for removal. (3) **Naming-collision gate**: Swift / Rust modules sharing a name (`agent_runtime`) must have an explicit `## Naming Distinction` block in CLAUDE.md FILE MAP. |
| **Falsifier (meta)** | `F-DualAPI-CanonicalPathDocumented` (**REFRAMED — registry surface is empty; falsifier premise unsatisfiable** — verified iter-147): the falsifier was authored against the iter-66 §21 dual-API list which named 3 instances. All 3 have since been reframed AWAY from being live dual-API: (1) `VaultSyncService` vs `VaultChatMutator` REFRAMED iter-126 — different responsibilities (sync/index vs diff-approval workflow), not dual; (2) `AppCoordinator` vs `AppBootstrap` REFRAMED iter-79 — orchestration on top, not competing composition root; (3) Swift `AgentRuntimeRegistry` vs Rust `agent_core::agent_runtime` REFRAMED iter-102 — Swift class is `@available(*, unavailable)` archive; only Rust path lives. **Net §21 dual-API live count: 0**. The falsifier's premise (maintain a `docs/canonical_path_registry.yaml` of live dual-API entries with primary-surface-receives-all-new-work gate) has no current surface to gate — the registry would be empty. If future dual-API instances emerge, file them in §21 first; the meta-falsifier becomes meaningful then. Build-next deferred (no work to do). `F-NamingCollision-DocumentedDistinction` (NOT IMPLEMENTED — confirmed by audit iter-147): `grep -iE "naming distinction\|naming collision\|naming convention" CLAUDE.md` returns 0 matches — no `## Naming Distinction` block exists. Live naming-collision candidates today (per iter-120 + iter-121 findings): (a) `pub struct MutationEnvelope` in agent_core vs graph-engine (different concepts, same name); (b) `pub struct Claim` in `agent_core/src/provenance/ledger.rs:179` vs `agent_core/src/resonance/mod.rs:67` (different concepts, same name). The falsifier's literal acceptance (block in CLAUDE.md) isn't met, but the §21 + §5g rows of THIS ledger explicitly document both — the explicit-documentation OR-clause is the doctrine being enforced. Build-next: either (a) add a `## Naming Distinction` block to CLAUDE.md citing both collisions, or (b) rename the resonance/graph-engine variants to remove the collisions (preferred — stronger structural fix). |
| **Cross-links** | [[VaultSyncService]] + [[VaultChatMutator]] (instance 1); [[AppBootstrap]] + [[AppCoordinator]] (instance 2 — covered in iter-48 row); [[AgentRuntimeRegistry]] (Swift) + [[agent_runtime]] (Rust) (instance 3); §20 god-state pattern (related — size; this — identity). |

**Summary — CI coverage per falsifier class**:

Verify the hash-gate logic actually skips work. (b) `scripts/check-perf-budgets.sh` is named like a perf-budget enforcement gate — verify it actually runs in CI and what budget thresholds it asserts (cross-row to [[HardwareTierManager]] M2 Pro floor). | **Falsifier** | `F-TiptapBundle-HashGateSkipsWork` (**PARTIAL — npm-install half is hash-gated, webpack-bundle half always re-runs; CLAUDE.md overstates the gate** — verified iter-141): the gate works for `npm ci` but NOT for webpack. `build-tiptap-bundle.sh:88-101` correctly computes `LOCK_HASH=$(shasum -a 256 package-lock.json \| cut -d' ' -f1)`, uses stamp file `node_modules/.installed-${LOCK_HASH}` (line 89), and **skips `npm ci`** when the stamp exists (line 91 `if [ ! -f "$STAMP_FILE" ]`). When package-lock.json hasn't changed, `npm ci` is correctly skipped. **But the webpack step at lines 107-111 runs unconditionally** — `npm run build -- --mode production` fires on every invocation regardless of hash. CLAUDE.md §"JS Bundle (Tiptap editor)" claims "content-hash gated on package-lock.json so unchanged checkouts skip the npm install + bundle steps" — the "+ bundle steps" half is doctrine-overstated; the script does NOT cache webpack output. **Plus**: no test asserts even the half that IS gated. Build-next: (a) update CLAUDE.md to "skips the npm install step" (drop "+ bundle"), OR (b) add a webpack-output-mtime gate that skips when `dist/index.js` is newer than every source file, OR (c) trust Xcode's preBuildScript invocation cache (timestamps based) which may absorb the webpack-runs-every-time cost at the Xcode level. Cheapest is doc fix (a). `F-PerfBudgets-CIWired` (**PASS by-construction** — verified iter-140): `.github/workflows/ci.yml:350-351` declares `- name: Check perf budgets (docs/perf-budgets.toml) run: ./scripts/check-perf-budgets.sh`. The CI step runs after `:343 Run morning-session bench (Wave 2.6)` produces `build/perf-budgets-runtime.json` (line 339-345 comment confirms the ordering rationale: runtime budgets need measured data not graceful-skip). Documented as ship-blocking per §23a CI Coverage Inventory line 1045: "Perf budgets at 350-351 (`./scripts/check-perf-budgets.sh` against `docs/perf-budgets.toml`)." Real CI gate; merge-blocking. `F-HeliosInvariants-CIWired` (**PASS by-construction** — verified iter-140): `.github/workflows/ci.yml:203` declares `- name: B5 — HELIOS theorem-invariant smoke (Canon Lock v2 §F) run: ./scripts/check-helios-invariants.sh`. Per the inline comment block (lines 198-201) the gate locks per-invariant sampling rates (E/H 1/100, PCF 1/10) with an aggregate ≤ 5 ms cumulative per inference budget. Both gates exit non-zero on regression — failures fail the workflow run. Documented in §23a CI Coverage Inventory. `F-ScriptsCacheNotInRepo` (**PARTIAL** — verified iter-117): the `.gitignore` half of the gate IS in place (`.gitignore` contains `__pycache__/` at file scope, so `git check-ignore` correctly ignores newly-created cache dirs), but a stale tracked `.pyc` remains in the index: `git ls-files \| grep __pycache__` returns `scripts/__pycache__/generate_reliability_matrix_tests.cpython-314.pyc` — added in commit `c99c6e577` ("pre-sync backup"), which predated the `.gitignore` entry. Once a file is tracked, `.gitignore` does not retro-untrack it; `git rm --cached scripts/__pycache__/generate_reliability_matrix_tests.cpython-314.pyc` closes the gap. Same shape as the `LSPServerProcess` historical-drift remediation pattern (CLAUDE.md §"LSP" commit `813c15dd`): canonical state is correct, one stale artifact needs removal. Build-next is a 2-line PR (`git rm --cached` + a `@Test`/CI grep gate asserting `git ls-files \| grep __pycache__` is empty). No CI gate currently enforces this so a future regression could re-track a `.pyc`. |

| **Missing proof** | (a) **Dual MutationEnvelope declarations confirmed AS NAMING COLLISION (worse than dual-API)** — iter-72 audit: `agent_core/src/mutations/envelope.rs:40` is the **canonical 14-field MutationEnvelope** (per §3.5 four-layer event hierarchy contract; `mutation_id`/`run_id`/etc., Swift mirror at `Epistemos/Models/MutationEnvelope.swift`). `graph-engine/src/knowledge_core/store.rs:57` is a **graph-engine-internal** struct with `tx_id`/`touched_block_ids`/`affects_summary/outline/backlinks/search/graph/body/ordering` describing what a transaction touched. **They are different concepts with the same name** — should be `GraphMutationEnvelope` or `KnowledgeCoreTransaction` in graph-engine to remove the collision. §21 meta-pattern: this is the *naming-collision* variant. (b) **`TypedArtifact` and `RunEventLog` are CANONICAL ALIASES**, not distinct types — iter-72 audit: `agent_core/src/scope_rex/answer_packet.rs:27-30` is the source-of-truth doctrine comment: "`TypedArtifact ≡ MutationEnvelope` (already in main), `RunEventLog ≡ provenance/ledger` (already in main), `ClaimFrame ≡ Claim`, `EvidenceLedger ≡ ClaimLedger`. AnswerPacket ties the four together at the chat-emission boundary." This resolves the canon-vs-code question: the substrate spine `TypedArtifact → MutationEnvelope → RunEventLog → ...` is *one* substrate stitched together by aliases, not 5 separate types. Surface this in CLAUDE.md FILE MAP with an explicit alias-mapping table. |
| **Next action** | Future tick: investigate `RunEventLog` + `TypedArtifact` location; investigate the dual `MutationEnvelope` declarations. Append W-row for canonical-event-type completeness audit. |
| **Falsifier** | `F-MutationEnvelope-NoDualDeclaration` (**PASS by-current-state + explicit-documentation** — verified iter-120): `grep -rn "^pub struct MutationEnvelope" agent_core/src/ graph-engine/src/` returns exactly **2 hits** — `agent_core/src/mutations/envelope.rs:40` (the canonical 14-field event-spine struct) and `graph-engine/src/knowledge_core/store.rs:57` (the graph-engine-internal tx-touched-set struct). `agent_core/src/scope_rex/answer_packet.rs:108 pub struct MutationEnvelopeId(pub String);` is a newtype ID wrapper, NOT a same-name redeclaration. Both clauses of the falsifier are satisfied: (i) exactly one declaration per crate; (ii) the dual-API is explicitly documented by THIS row's Missing-proof + Evidence fields and by §21 dual-API meta-pattern. **Caveat**: iter-72 audit re-classified this as a **naming collision** (different concepts sharing the name) rather than a true dual-API (same concept exposed twice) — the literal falsifier wording was authored before that distinction was understood. A stricter follow-up falsifier `F-MutationEnvelope-NoNamingCollision` (rename graph-engine's struct to `GraphMutationEnvelope` or `KnowledgeCoreTransaction`) is the build-next candidate; until then, this row's documentation IS the falsifier's "explicit documentation" escape clause. Gap (PASS-by-state not PASS-by-construction): no CI grep-gate enforces the "exactly 2 declarations" count on future PRs. `F-CanonicalEventTypes-Completeness` (**PASS by-source-doctrine + struct-verification** — verified iter-121, restored after iter-120 inadvertently dropped the falsifier from this cell): substrate spine `TypedArtifact → MutationEnvelope → RunEventLog → {AgentEvent, GraphEvent} → UI projection` — every named type is either a `pub struct` in the workspace OR an explicit alias to a `pub struct`. Source-of-truth alias doctrine at `agent_core/src/scope_rex/answer_packet.rs:27-30`: `TypedArtifact ≡ MutationEnvelope`, `RunEventLog ≡ provenance/ledger` (i.e., ClaimLedger), `ClaimFrame ≡ Claim`, `EvidenceLedger ≡ ClaimLedger`. Struct verification: `pub struct MutationEnvelope` at `agent_core/src/mutations/envelope.rs:40` ✓, `pub struct AgentEvent` at `epistemos-core/src/agent_runtime.rs:23` ✓, `pub struct GraphEvent` at `substrate-rt/src/graph_event.rs:46` ✓, `pub struct Claim` at `agent_core/src/provenance/ledger.rs:179` ✓, `pub struct ClaimLedger` at `agent_core/src/provenance/ledger.rs:409` ✓. UI projection = Swift consumers enumerated in this row's Evidence cell. **Side finding**: a SECOND `pub struct Claim` exists at `agent_core/src/resonance/mod.rs:67` — same naming-collision shape as MutationEnvelope (iter-120). Either rename the resonance variant to `ResonanceClaim` or document the dual-API; provisional follow-up `F-Claim-NoNamingCollision` is the build-next candidate. Gap: no CI doc-walker enforces the alias-doctrine list — build-next is a `cargo test` that parses the `answer_packet.rs` alias comment and asserts every referenced type compiles. |

Byte-equal output at temperature=0 is architecturally infeasible because: (1) Quantization kernels differ (GGUF `q4_k_m` 6-bit-scale 256-weight blocks vs MLX `mlx-4bit-w-int4-zero-fp16`); (2) Matmul kernels differ (`ggml_mul_mat_q4_K` vs MLX Metal-compute matmul; FMA-order differences → different rounding); (3) Sampling kernels differ in softmax numerical-stability shifts.
